(https://github.com/grpc/grpc-go/blob/master/rpc_util.go#L319-L323)\n   241→type EtcdError struct {\n   242→\tcode codes.Code\n   243→\tdesc string\n   244→}\n   245→\n   246→// Code returns grpc/codes.Code.\n   247→// TODO: define clientv3/codes.Code.\n   248→func (e EtcdError) Code() codes.Code {\n   249→\treturn e.code\n   250→}\n   251→\n   252→func (e EtcdError) Error() string {\n   253→\treturn e.desc\n   254→}\n   255→\n   256→func Error(err error) error {\n   257→\tif err == nil {\n   258→\t\treturn nil\n   259→\t}\n   260→\tverr, ok := errStringToError[ErrorDesc(err)]\n   261→\tif !ok { // not gRPC error\n   262→\t\treturn err\n   263→\t}\n   264→\tev, ok := status.FromError(verr)\n   265→\tvar desc string\n   266→\tif ok {\n   267→\t\tdesc = ev.Message()\n   268→\t} else {\n   269→\t\tdesc = verr.Error()\n   270→\t}\n   271→\treturn EtcdError{code: ev.Code(), desc: desc}\n   272→}\n   273→\n   274→func ErrorDesc(err error) string {\n   275→\tif s, ok := status.FromError(err); ok {\n   276→\t\treturn s.Message()\n   277→\t}\n   278→\treturn err.Error()\n   279→}\n   280→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it \"text\": \"## gRPC Error Status Propagation Across Go Services\\n\\n### etcd-io/etcd\\netcd demonstrates a comprehensive error mapping architecture. The central hub is `api/v3rpc/rpctypes/error.go` which creates gRPC Status errors using `status.Error()` with specific gRPC codes. This file defines errors like `ErrGRPCLeaseNotFound` with `codes.NotFound`, `ErrGRPCInvalidArgument` with `codes.InvalidArgument`, and `ErrGRPCUnavailable` with `codes.Unavailable`. The file creates a two-tier error system: server-side gRPC errors and client-side errors that unwrap gRPC Status objects.\\n\\nThe error propagation chain flows through `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/util.go`, which implements the `togRPCError()` function. This function contains `toGRPCErrorMap`, a mapping from internal server errors (from membership, auth, mvcc, lease packages) to pre-defined gRPC status errors. All gRPC service implementations (`auth.go`, `key.go`, `lease.go`, `watch.go`) call `togRPCError()` to convert internal errors before returning them from RPC methods.\\n\\nFor HTTP/gRPC gateway translation, etcd uses generated gateway files (`api/etcdserverpb/gw/rpc.pb.gw.go`, `server/etcdserver/api/v3election/v3electionpb/gw/v3election.pb.gw.go`, `server/etcdserver/api/v3lock/v3lockpb/gw/v3lock.pb.gw.go`) created by grpc-gateway. These files use `status.Errorf(codes.InvalidArgument)` for validation errors and delegate HTTP response generation to the grpc-gateway runtime.\\n\\nOn the client side, `client/v3/retry_interceptor.go` implements a retry interceptor that inspects gRPC error codes to determine if errors are retryable, checking against codes like `codes.Unavailable` and context errors.\\n\\n### kubernetes/kubernetes\\nKubernetes takes a more distributed approach to gRPC error handling without a centralized error mapping. Key implementations include:\\n\\n**Rate Limiting**: `pkg/kubelet/apis/grpc/ratelimit.go` creates a static error `ErrorLimitExceeded = status.Error(codes.ResourceExhausted, \\\"rejected by rate limit\\\")` in a rate-limiting unary server interceptor (`LimiterUnaryServerInterceptor`).\\n\\n**Probing**: `pkg/probe/grpc/grpc.go` implements health checking that extracts gRPC status codes using `status.FromError()` and inspects specific codes like `codes.Unimplemented` and `codes.DeadlineExceeded` to provide detailed error messages.\\n\\n**CRI (Container Runtime Interface) Error Handling**: `staging/src/k8s.io/cri-api/pkg/errors/errors.go` provides utility functions like `IsNotFound()` that check if an error is a gRPC `codes.NotFound` error by using `status.FromError()` and comparing the code.\\n\\n**Kubelet Runtime**: `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_container.go` imports gRPC codes for error handling in container operations, and `pkg/volume/csi/csi_client.go` uses gRPC status codes to interpret CSI plugin errors.\\n\\nKubernetes does not use a centralized error mapping like etcd; instead, it checks error codes at the point of use and converts them to Kubernetes-specific error types or logging messages.\\n\\n### grafana/grafana\\nGrafana uses gRPC errors primarily in plugin and service mesh components:\\n\\n**Request Status Tracking**: `pkg/plugins/instrumentationutils/request_status.go` contains `RequestStatusFromError()` that extracts gRPC status codes using `grpcstatus.FromError()` and checks for `codes.Canceled` and `codes.DeadlineExceeded` to categorize request status (ok, cancelled, error).\\n\\n**gRPC Interceptors**: `pkg/services/grpcserver/interceptors/auth.go` creates `status.Error(codes.Unauthenticated)` errors in the `tokenAuth()` method when token validation fails, serving as an authentication interceptor.\\n\\n**Authorization Service**: `pkg/services/authz/zanzana/server/server_batch_check.go` uses `status.Errorf(grpccodes.InvalidArgument)` to return validation errors when batch check items exceed the maximum count.\\n\\n**Plugin Architecture**: `pkg/plugins/backendplugin/grpcplugin/client_v2.go` and `pkg/plugins/manager/client/client.go` handle gRPC client operations with error code inspection.\\n\\n**HTTP/Resource Error Mapping**: `pkg/storage/unified/resource/errors.go` demonstrates HTTP status code mapping by converting errors to `resourcepb.ErrorResult` with HTTP status codes like `http.StatusConflict` (409), `http.StatusBadRequest` (400), and `http.StatusNotFound` (404), creating a bridge between gRPC/API errors and HTTP responses.\\n\\n### Error Propagation Patterns\\n\\n**etcd Pattern**: Centralized error definition (`error.go`) → Error mapping function (`togRPCError()`) → Service method implementation → Pre-defined status errors with codes → gRPC-gateway for HTTP translation.\\n\\n**Kubernetes Pattern**: Distributed error handling → Per-component error code checking → Service-specific error handling (no centralized mapping) → REST API error translation in apiserver handlers.\\n\\n**Grafana Pattern**: Interceptor-based error creation → Status code checking at inspection points → Plugin SDK integration → HTTP status code mapping in resource layer.\\n\\nAll three projects use `google.golang.org/grpc/status` and `google.golang.org/grpc/codes` packages for creating and inspecting gRPC errors. The main differences lie in centralization (etcd's mapped approach vs Kubernetes' distributed approach) and HTTP translation mechanism (etcd uses grpc-gateway, Kubernetes uses REST handlers, Grafana uses custom HTTP mappings in the resource layer).\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3378,"cache_read_input_tokens":64455,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3378},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"795a64f0-33ad-4321-8d75-dfd171d7b313","uuid":"e8a692e4-e949-434b-bbe6-36b437bbf3e1"}
